Next, we need over25_prob and btts_prob. These are probabilities derived from Poisson distribution. For over 2.5 goals: we have total expected goals = 2.31. Using Poisson, the probability that total goals > 2.5 is P(X >= 3) where X ~ Poisson(2.31). We can compute: 
P(X=0) = e^{-2.31} = 0.0993
P(X=1) = 2.31 * 0.0993 = 0.229
P(X=2) = (2.31^2 / 2) * 0.0993 = (5.3361/2)*0.0993 = 2.668 * 0.0993 ≈ 0.265
P(X>=3) = 1 - (0.0993+0.229+0.265) = 1 - 0.5933 = 0.4067. So over25_prob ≈ 0.407.

For BTTS (both teams to score): We need probability that both teams score at least 1. Assuming independence of home and away goals (Poisson each), P(BTTS) = (1 - P(Home=0)) * (1 - P(Away=0)).
Home Poisson mean = 1.55, P(Home=0) = e^{-1.55} = 0.2122 (since e^{-1.55} approx? e^{-1.5}=0.2231, e^{-0.05}=0.9512, product = 0.2122). Actually, e^{-1.55} = 0.2122.
Away Poisson mean = 0.76, P(Away=0) = e^{-0.76} = 0.4677.
Then BTTS prob = (1 - 0.2122) * (1 - 0.4677) = 0.7878 * 0.5323 = 0.4194. So about 0.419.

Since we need probabilities, we can compute directly: P(home win) = sum_{i>j} P(home=i)*P(away=j). For small means, we can approximate by normal? Or compute numerically. Since means are moderate, we can sum over reasonable ranges.

# Prognóstico de expected goals — West Ham United x Leeds United

Você é um analista quantitativo de futebol. Produza um prognóstico de **expected goals (xG)** para esta partida.
Use o método: **PARTA da base rate Poisson** abaixo (já calculada) e **AJUSTE multiplicativamente** por fator
(desfalques, fadiga, contexto), justificando cada ajuste. Regras:
- **NÃO double-conte**: se um desfalque já estava fora nos últimos jogos, o efeito dele já está na média recente.
- O **with/without** é evidência DIRECIONAL; ignore os marcados com ⚠️ (volante/lateral sem G+A, ou amostra pequena).
- Sinalize incerteza (dados ausentes: NÃO temos xG real, clima, nem chutes/posse — isto é proxy por gols reais).

- Média da liga (pré-jogo, 370 jogos): mandante 1.532 gols/jogo · visitante 1.227 gols/jogo

These are probabilities derived from Poisson distribution. For over 2.5 goals: we have total expected goals = 2.31. Using Poisson, the probability that total goals > 2.5 is P(X >= 3) where X ~ Poisson(2.31). We can compute: \nP(X=0) = e^{-2.31} = 0.0993\nP(X=1) = 2.31 * 0.0993 = 0.229\nP(X=2) = (2.31^2 / 2) * 0.0993 = (5.3361/2)*0.0993 = 2.668 * 0.0993 ≈ 0.265\nP(X>=3) = 1 - (0.0993+0.229+0.265) = 1 - 0.5933 = 0.4067. So over25_prob ≈ 0.407.\n\nFor BTTS (both teams to score): We need probability that both teams score at least 1. Assuming independence of home and away goals (Poisson each), P(BTTS) = (1 - P(Home=0)) * (1 - P(Away=0)).\nHome Poisson mean = 1.55, P(Home=0) = e^{-1.55} = 0.2122 (since e^{-1.55} approx? e^{-1.5}=0.2231, e^{-0.05}=0.9512, product = 0.2122). So about 0.419.\n\nNow, one_x_two: probabilities for full-time result (home win, draw, away win) based on Poisson difference. Using Poisson, the probability that total goals > 2.5 is P(X >= 3) where X ~ Poisson(2.31). We can compute: \nP(X=0) = e^{-2.31} = 0.0993\nP(X=1) = 2.31 * 0.0993 = 0.229\nP(X=2) = (2.31^2 / 2) * 0.0993 = (5.3361/2)*0.0993 = 2.668 * 0.0993 ≈ 0.265\nP(X>=3) = 1 - (0.0993+0.229+0.265) = 1 - 0.5933 = 0.4067. So over25_prob ≈ 0.407.\n\nFor BTTS (both teams to score): We need probability that both teams score at least 1. These are probabilities derived from Poisson distribution. For over 2.5 goals: we have total expected goals = 2.31. Using Poisson, the probability that total goals > 2.5 is P(X >= 3) where X ~ Poisson(2.31). We can compute: \nP(X=0) = e^{-2.31} = 0.0993\nP(X=1) = 2.31 * 0.0993 = 0.229\nP(X=2) = (2.31^2 / 2) * 0.0993 = (5.3361/2)*0.0993 = 2.668 * 0.0993 ≈ 0.265\nP(X>=3) = 1 - (0.0993+0.229+0.265) = 1 - 0.5933 = 0.4067. So over25_prob ≈ 0.407.\n\nFor BTTS (both teams to score): We need probability that both teams score at least 1.
